# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# etcd Raft Snapshot Too Old on Node Rejoin

## Your Task

An etcd node fails to rejoin a cluster with 'ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable'. Find the Go source files in etcd-io/etcd that (1) define ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable and (2) implement the snapshot availability check during Raft log catch-up.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

92-assistanttext-
I've completed my search through the etcd-io/etcd repository and created a comprehensive answer at `/workspace/answer.json`. 

**Key Findings:**

While I conducted an extensive search, I was unable to locate an error specifically named "ErrSnapshotTemporarilyUnavailable" in the current etcd codebase. However, I identified the **critical files and mechanisms** involved in snapshot availability checking during Raft log catch-up:

1. **server/etcdserver/api/snap/snapshotter.go** - Defines `ErrNoSnapshot` and `LoadNewestAvailable()` method used to check if a usable snapshot exists

2. **server/etcdserver/api/rafthttp/http.go** - Contains the `snapshotHandler` that processes incoming snapshot messages and performs Process() checks that can return availability errors

3. **server/etcdserver/server.go** - Implements the `Process()` method for Raft message handling and `snapshotIfNeededAndCompactRaftLog()` for snapshot management

4. **server/config/config.go** and **server/embed/config.go** - Define `SnapshotCatchUpEntries` configuration (default 5000 entries) that determines the log catch-up window

The snapshot availability check occurs during the Raft log catch-up process: when a node with a too-old snapshot attempts to rejoin and cannot catch up within the `SnapshotCatchUpEntries` window, an availability error is returned.

The error you mentioned may be newly added or defined differently in a newer version of the codebase.

Or we have to wait for\\n35: \\t// tcp keepalive failing to detect a bad connection, which is at minutes level.\\n36: \\t// For long term streaming connections, rafthttp pkg sends application level linkHeartbeatMessage\\n37: \\t// to keep the connection alive.\\n38: \\t// For short term pipeline connections, the connection MUST be killed to avoid it being\\n39: \\t// put back to http pkg connection pool.\\n40: \\tDefaultConnReadTimeout  = 5 * time.Second\\n41: \\tDefaultConnWriteTimeout = 5 * time.Second\\n42: \\n43: \\trecvBufSize = 4096\\n44: \\t// maxPendingProposals holds the proposals during one leader election process.\\n45: \\t// Generally one leader election takes at most 1 sec. When a follower node falls behind the leader, the system may need to send a snapshot to help the node catch up. The key components involved are: (1) **Snapshot Error Definition** (server/etcdserver/api/snap/snapshotter.go): The ErrNoSnapshot error is defined here and represents when no snapshot is available. The LoadNewestAvailable method loads the newest snapshot that matches WAL snapshot entries, which is used during recovery. (2) **Snapshot Message Handling** (server/etcdserver/api/rafthttp/http.go): The snapshotHandler.ServeHTTP method receives snapshot messages from the leader and processes them. It calls h.r.Process() which can return a writerToResponse error if snapshot availability checks fail. (3) **Raft Message Processing** (server/etcdserver/server.go): The Process method (line 706) validates incoming Raft messages and delegates to r.Step(). The snapshotIfNeededAndCompactRaftLog function manages snapshot creation and compaction based on SnapshotCatchUpEntries. (4) **Configuration** (server/config/config.go, server/embed/config.go): SnapshotCatchUpEntries is the critical configuration that determines how many entries are kept after snapshotting to allow slow followers to catch up without needing a snapshot. DefaultSnapshotCatchUpEntries is set to 5000 (server/etcdserver/server.go line 83). When a node with an old snapshot attempts to rejoin (where its snapshot index is older than the entries available for log catch-up), the system cannot provide the necessary entries to synchronize. This triggers snapshot availability validation during message processing. The snapshot availability check ensures that the follower's log can be brought into sync either through entry replication (if within SnapshotCatchUpEntries) or through snapshot transfer (if the node is too far behind).\"\n}\n",
